  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a265865f-485b-4736-89e2-01328955de06'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText17260170299064656625" style="display:none"><i>Who knows you well? Your best friend? Your boyfriend or girlfriend? A stranger you meet on a crazy night? No one, really?</i><br /><br />Mark and Kate have sat next to each other for an entire year, but have never spoken. For whatever reason, their paths outside of class have never crossed.<br /><br />That is, until Kate spots Mark miles away from home, out in the city for a wild, unexpected night. Kate is lost, having just run away from a chance to finally meet the girl she has been in love with from afar. Mark, meanwhile, is in love with his best friend Ryan, who may or may not feel the same way.<br /><br />When Kate and Mark meet up, little do they know how important they will become to each other—and how, in a very short time, they will know each other better than any of the people who are supposed to know them more.<br /><br />Told in alternating points of view by Nina LaCour and David Levithan, <i>You Know Me Well</i> is a story about navigating the joys and heartaches of first love, one truth at a time.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1627373723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17806918085498555684"><blockquote>
  <em>I guess Katie and I have formed our own rainbow alliance. It feels like she’s something </em>
  <em>I’ve always wanted but didn’t know I wanted until I got it: a partner in crime.</em>
</blockquote><br/><br/><em> </em><strong>I don’t want to write a single word. I will, but it pains me to. </strong>You see, I thought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' title='David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a> and I had this connection. We used to bond fairly well and just… understand one another. He amazed me.<br/><br/>Now I’m not so sure anymore. I don’t know <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour' title='Nina LaCour' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina LaCour</a>—haven’t read anything by her—but I don’t think her co-writing this boo</span>
  <span id="freeText17806918085498555684" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>I guess Katie and I have formed our own rainbow alliance. It feels like she’s something </em>
  <em>I’ve always wanted but didn’t know I wanted until I got it: a partner in crime.</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em> </em><strong>I don’t want to write a single word. I will, but it pains me to. </strong>You see, I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> and I had this connection. We used to bond fairly well and just… understand one another. He amazed me.<br /><br />Now I’m not so sure anymore. I don’t know <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour" title="Nina LaCour" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina LaCour</a>—haven’t read anything by her—but I don’t think her co-writing this book is the problem.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27158835.You_Know_Me_Well" title="You Know Me Well by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">You Know Me Well</a> is <strong>so incredibly inauthentic</strong>.<br /><br />So we have Mark and Kate. They’re not friends. YET, in the span of one night, they become the best buddies the planet Earth has seen. <strong>They have nothing in common, e</strong>xcept, maybe, the fact that they’re both gay and afraid of love.<br /><br /><blockquote> <em>‘You’ve never told him,’ Violet says. It’s not a question. It’s obvious. ‘I tell him all the time—I just make sure it’s never when he’s listening. I say it when he’s in the other room, or when he’s asleep, or when the music’s really loud. Sometimes he asks me what I just said. And I tell him never mind. Or I make up something else, something that isn’t ‘I love you.’</em></blockquote><br /><br /><em> </em>Mark has been in love with his best friend—sometimes friend with benefits—Ryan <strong>FOR YEARS</strong>. But he never had the courage to tell him. Kate is crazy about this one girl named Violet who she never met but has heard so much about by her best friend whom, may I add, she doesn’t even truly consider as a ‘real friend.’<br /><br />Somehow, Mark and Kate <strong>JUST CONNECT</strong>. Just like that. They meet, and they click. It’s like insta-friendship. Normally I do tend to believe in that—hey, I’m not that cynical—but for two people to become<em> intimate</em> friends after only a couple of hours spent together? <strong>That doesn’t work for me. </strong>They barely know anything about one another. Hell, Kate, Mark could have been a psycho, for all you knew!<br /><br /><blockquote> <em>‘Admit it,’ Violet says. ‘You could both use a little clarity in your lives.’</em><br /><em>And ever though I have done enough soul-searching for the night, I know that I can’t let Violet down again, so <strong>I grab Mark’s hand and lead him over</strong>.</em></blockquote><br /><br /><em> </em>Did I mention that Kate is madly crazy about Violet, so much that she stressed out her life the night she was supposed to meet her and bailed? So <strong>why does she continuously drag Mark along everywhere she goes? </strong>It’s supposed to be Kate and Violet’s date, but Mark is always there. It was hard for this book to be romantic, when the authors focused so much on the insta-friendship between Mark and Kate.<br /><br /><blockquote> <em>‘Maybe I just moved too fast for you,’ she says. ‘Maybe it was stupid for me to kiss you like that. ‘No,’ I say. ‘It was amazing. It was the most romantic moment of my life. I’ve replayed it thousands of times since it happened. I want to kiss you again. Please trust me. I want to kiss you right now, but you deserve to be kissed by someone who has her shit together. So I’m going to get my shit together, and then, if you still want me, I’m going to kiss you.</em></blockquote><br /><br /><strong><em> </em>Wait, is that supposed to be romantic? </strong>That paragraph is made of clichés. If you remove those, there’s literally nothing left.<br /><br />Another thing that characterizes this book as inauthentic is Mark’s rapidly falling out of love. As I mentioned, he has been in love with Ryan <em>for a very long time,</em> but the latter never thought of him in that way. Sure, they’re fooling around, but it’s nothing deep and serious. When Ryan finds someone else to fool around with, Mark feels angry, betrayed and so, so sad. Yet, in the span of a couple of days, he just… accepts it and ‘moves on’. <strong>WHAT THE HELL.</strong><br /><br /><strong> </strong>He’s your best friend. You’re madly in love with him. You want him to be your boyfriend—that’s what you’ve always wanted. Don’t come telling me that seeing him with someone else doesn’t shatter your bones. Don’t come telling me that you can just go on with your life and participate in activities with both Ryan and his new boyfriend, <strong>JUST LIKE THAT</strong>. Hell, there’s a reason why most people don’t stay friends after they’ve broken up, but that’s what Mark and Ryan do. Maybe they weren’t boyfriends per se, but Mark took their friends-with-benefits relationship very seriously.<br /><br />One last thing that disappointed me: the repetition. Alright, I’ll admit that the writing style is lyrical and reads beautifully, but I bet the story would have had four less chapters had there not been so much repetition. I’m not going to provide you with an example, because the quotes I’ve shared already give you a good idea.<br /><br /><strong>NAY TO THE BOOK, BUT YAY LGBT.</strong><br /><br /><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17806918085498555684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2440533730" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2440533730" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2440533730?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781925355529" href="/book/show/29907469-you-know-me-well">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lesbian-mc">lesbian-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=gay-mc">gay-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=f-f">f-f</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2440533730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8630187914840118032"><i>
  <blockquote>“I'm ready to love myself, but I'm not ready to lose you. <br/>I'm ready to find myself, but I'm not ready for you to know what I find” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>This book had the most iconic mlm/wlw solidarity and I am HERE FOR IT. To be honest, this was the exact kind of queer book I needed and I didn't even realise that until I read it. I loved the friendship between Mark and Kate, a lesbian and gay character and just how this whole book played out. I read it pretty much in one sitting and enjoyed all of it so much. <br/><br/><b>Yo</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8630187914840118032" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“I'm ready to love myself, but I'm not ready to lose you. <br>I'm ready to find myself, but I'm not ready for you to know what I find” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>This book had the most iconic mlm/wlw solidarity and I am HERE FOR IT. To be honest, this was the exact kind of queer book I needed and I didn't even realise that until I read it. I loved the friendship between Mark and Kate, a lesbian and gay character and just how this whole book played out. I read it pretty much in one sitting and enjoyed all of it so much. <br><br><b>You Know Me Well</b> follows Kate and Mark, who sit next to eachother in class and never talk. They run into eachother in the city one night and realise, over one wild night, that they do have some things on common. Kate is in love with a girl she barely knows, and Mark is in love wish his best best friend Ryan who may or may not know. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537793779i/26346616.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537793779i/26346617.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The friendship between Mark and Kate was my favourite thing about this. I always say queer people travel in packs and the friendship between the two really resonated with me. I related to them both a lot, but also felt quite Seen because it's really rare to have queer friends in books. I really liked the focus on the formative years of identity, and how being in that stage of your life where you're trying to find yourself is complicated so much by also trying to understand your queer identity. <br><br>This is an ownvoices book and you can tell. Nina LaCour and David Levithan perfectly capture what their characters and the idea of Pride. This book is set over the week of Pride in San Francisco and I love how they explored the entire queer community and the idea of spaces being welcoming and safe the first time you enter them. I also really related to Mark and his struggle with having a crush on your friend and not knowing what to do about it. This book was extremely powerful and relatable and I really loved that about it. <br><br>Pacing wise, this is also perfect. Its easy to read in one sitting because something is always happening. The authors used the dual perspective so effectively, always leaving each chapter hanging so you were excited to read both narrations. I can easily say I was equally interested in both Kate and Mark's story. <br><br>My one criticism is that Kate's love interest was a little panic pixie dream girl. I think it was kind of addressed a bit so it wasn't too bad but I think adding more depth and complexity to her character would have been really beneficial to her character. <br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“You're becoming. You're in the process of becoming. You just don't know what yet.<br>That felt right. It felt okay to stop there, for now, as we walked through the future.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I really liked this book. It's unlike so many other contemporary books on the market right now. This book perfectly encapsulates why ownvoices books are so good. I loved the friendships in this so much and the romances were pretty perfect too. Nina LaCour and David Levithan captured so many of my emotions in this and the events resonated with me so much. I really recommend this if you're looking for a quick read with a gay/lesbian character</span>
  <a data-text-id="8630187914840118032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508263707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18181923537520934001"><i>"I'm ready to lose myself,<br/>but I'm not ready to lose you.<br/>I'm ready to find myself,<br/>But I'm not ready for you to know what I find."</i><br/><br/>This was my first book by Nina LaCour and my fifth by David Levithan (and compared to the other 4 books I've read I liked this one best).<br/><i>You Know Me Well</i> is one of those books that you can easily read in one sitting. It has a great pace, relatable characters and never once gets boring. It's also incredibly romantic.<br/>I have nothing to criticise. I enjoyed this a lot. It's</span>
  <span id="freeText18181923537520934001" style="display:none"><i>"I'm ready to lose myself,<br />but I'm not ready to lose you.<br />I'm ready to find myself,<br />But I'm not ready for you to know what I find."</i><br /><br />This was my first book by Nina LaCour and my fifth by David Levithan (and compared to the other 4 books I've read I liked this one best).<br /><i>You Know Me Well</i> is one of those books that you can easily read in one sitting. It has a great pace, relatable characters and never once gets boring. It's also incredibly romantic.<br />I have nothing to criticise. I enjoyed this a lot. It's a wonderful story about friendship and love, that I would recommend to everyone who wants a heartfelt but light read.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_2479257733" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2479257733" />
    <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez"><img alt="Claudia Ramírez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533869692p2/13061577.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2479257733?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia Ramírez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia Ramírez" href="/user/show/13061577-claudia-ram-rez">Claudia Ramírez</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_1419823208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1419823208" />
    <a title="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd"><img alt="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539540436p2/5138611.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1419823208?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)" href="/user/show/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd">Cece (ProblemsOfaBookNerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=anticipated-of-2016">anticipated-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5138611-cece-problemsofabooknerd?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1419823208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16325812277542242576">*2.5/5<br/><br/>I'm so sad to be writing that I gave this book 2.5 stars. This was my most anticipated release of 2016, by two authors I adore. It is #ownvoices and stuffed to the brim with queer characters and it should have been perfect for me. But it wasn't.<br/><br/>Stuff I loved: <br/>-How Pride was written. Every scene that was more focused on Pride than the characters themselves was well done and fun to read. <br/>-The attention to queer spaces as safe spaces, and the fact that there was an acknowledgement that older </span>
  <span id="freeText16325812277542242576" style="display:none">*2.5/5<br /><br />I'm so sad to be writing that I gave this book 2.5 stars. This was my most anticipated release of 2016, by two authors I adore. It is #ownvoices and stuffed to the brim with queer characters and it should have been perfect for me. But it wasn't.<br /><br />Stuff I loved: <br />-How Pride was written. Every scene that was more focused on Pride than the characters themselves was well done and fun to read. <br />-The attention to queer spaces as safe spaces, and the fact that there was an acknowledgement that older queer people are there to look out for younger queer/questioning people. There is a scene at the beginning where Kate describes going into a gay bar and feeling totally safe and I adored that.<br />-Bits and pieces of just queer culture. The constant inclusion of specific queer girl bands that really resonated with me. I loved those elements that made the whole book and the characters feel specifically queer, not just queer to have a queer main character. It felt like part of their characterization that was essential. If that makes any sense at all.<br />-Every. single. character. that had a line (besides parents) was queer. Every one of them. And coming from YA, where the main character can be queer but everyone else around them is straight? It felt like a miracle. It also felt like the first realistic depiction of queer kids in high school, in their friendships at least.<br /><br />Stuff I didn't love:<br />-The main pixie dream girl love interest. I kept waiting for it to... not be that. But she stayed manic pixie to the end and I didn't understand the relationship at all.<br />-Honestly, Kate as a character. I can't handle when miscommunication or just lack of any communication at all leads to tension and causes angst moving forward. It isn't compelling to me, and that's just about all Kate had to offer. <br />-The dramatic monologues. None of the lines in this entire book were realistic. And yes, this is a book and I can't hold it to 100% authentic standards, but these kids were ridiculously poetic every time they spoke. And don't get me started on when Mark would go all poetic for paragraphs. I don't think it ever made sense for his character.<br /><br />Overall, I think this book could have benefited from a) being longer and b) not trying quite so hard to be meaningful. That sounds harsh when I write it. But honestly, I wanted to read a book about two queer kids finding one another and just having that friendship be valuable. I didn't need it to change my life. I just wanted a story that was gay and happy. And I felt like this book tried to do too many things, so they all individually fell flat. Now, if you don't mind, I'm going to go cry about how much I wanted to love this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16325812277542242576" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14669836139863289953"><br/>I’m afraid to say but this book has finally made me realize that Mr. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan' title='David Levithan' rel='nofollow noopener'>David Levithan</a> and I should officially call it quits. Like I said, his writing is always thoughtful and beautiful but there’s just always something in his stories that makes a premise with great potential become quite too unrealistic. I don’t know how much of the story is on Ms. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Nina%20La%20Cour' title='Nina La Cour' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina La Cour</a> but I’m still giving her a chance with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6373717.Hold_Still' title='Hold Still by Nina LaCour' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hold Still</a>. <br/><br/>I’m not discouraging people to read this though because it could still be a quick, enjo</span>
  <span id="freeText14669836139863289953" style="display:none"><br />I’m afraid to say but this book has finally made me realize that Mr. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/11664.David_Levithan" title="David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">David Levithan</a> and I should officially call it quits. Like I said, his writing is always thoughtful and beautiful but there’s just always something in his stories that makes a premise with great potential become quite too unrealistic. I don’t know how much of the story is on Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=Nina%20La%20Cour" title="Nina La Cour" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina La Cour</a> but I’m still giving her a chance with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6373717.Hold_Still" title="Hold Still by Nina LaCour" rel="nofollow noopener">Hold Still</a>. <br /><br />I’m not discouraging people to read this though because it could still be a quick, enjoyable read if you look past the unrealistic elements. ;)<br /></span>

    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1675014833" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16771218793942191045">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a> <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644515.gif' alt='Palm Springs commercial photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Is this the beginning of the end? Am I officially getting too old for this shit???? Say it ain’t so!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! <br/><br/>I refuse to believe that could be the case. Instead I’m going to blame the “meh” factor on (1) I’m in a horrible book slump and not really loving much of anything; (2) NetGalley is all-knowing and I should listen to them when they deny me a request instead of immediately putting myself on the library waiting list lik</span>
  <span id="freeText16771218793942191045" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a> <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644515.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Is this the beginning of the end? Am I officially getting too old for this shit???? Say it ain’t so!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! <br><br>I refuse to believe that could be the case. Instead I’m going to blame the “meh” factor on (1) I’m in a horrible book slump and not really loving much of anything; (2) NetGalley is all-knowing and I should listen to them when they deny me a request instead of immediately putting myself on the library waiting list like a pouty two year old; and (3) I’ve read a better version of this already . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644516.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Ha! Fooled you. That’s actually from <i>Youth In Revolt</i>, but I love the quote so I put it here. Also, Michael Cera has played the exact same character in every G.D. thing he’s ever been in, so really I could’ve posted that or a George Michael gif or one from Juno or this one that actually applies . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644517.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yeah, so <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/701969521?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Nick and Norah</a> (man, I kinda ranted like a loon over a pretty decent teeny bopper selection with that one) and also <i>Will Grayson, Will Grayson</i> and probably even <i>Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares</i> (not positive since I own it in the book hoard but have not ever bothered to read it) were better to me than this one. The special Levithan Kool-Aid must have been watered down. *shrug*<br><br><i>You Know Me Well</i> is the story of Mark and Kate. Although the two have gone to school together for eternity, they have never really met. That is, until one night when Kate’s nerves get to her and she runs away from meeting the potential girl of her dreams and sees Mark dancing in his underpants on a bar. One thing leads to another and Kate discovers that although Mark pines for his friendship with Ryan to go to the next level and for them to DTR, unfortunately . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644518.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Annnnnnnnnnnnnnnnnnnnnd that’s where it lost me. I’m all for unrequited love and whathaveyou, but there wasn’t a whole lot of substance to this one. Kate came off as a neurotic a-hole half the time - Mark was a bit of a creeper who refused to see the truth that Ryan might be okay with coming out, he just didn’t want to come out with Mark - they lived in pretty much Utopia, USA where everyone was middle-class and the parents/everyone in high school was super accepting of all things LBGTQ (which would be amazing, but let’s face it, is not the current reality). It did have a handful of fairly awesome quotable quotes . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“I don’t want to be a best friend if I can’t also be a boy in his eyes. I don’t want to be a calendar if I’ll never get a date.”</i>
</b><br><br>But sadly they weren’t enough to boost my rating. I think Levithan has fallen into the same trap as Rainbow Rowell. They both need to JUST SLOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOW DOWN. There’s no reason to churn out not-so-great books just for the sake of churning them out. Take your time and write something a little deeper. Your real fans will wait for you. Now, here is an adorable kitten gif for all of you youngsters who are getting your pitchforks and torches ready to go . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467904027ra/19644519.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Please don’t troll me. Thanks in advance : ) </span>
  <a data-text-id="16771218793942191045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509823932" href="/book/show/29848950-you-know-me-well">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2857565460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9279432473870504691">Just shout out to me for reading a book SET in Pride month actually <i>during</i> Pride month. 😌that's the kind of timing i could never plan, my friends, it only happens on accident. I am just that disorganised. <i>Anyhow</i>, my miraculous timing aside, this was <b>basically the best thing</b> and I am utterly soft for this book. Yessss the romance was a bit fast but like I shall fling all negativity into the sea and just dissolve myself into this book where people can just meet the perfect friend, the perfect girl</span>
  <span id="freeText9279432473870504691" style="display:none">Just shout out to me for reading a book SET in Pride month actually <i>during</i> Pride month. 😌that's the kind of timing i could never plan, my friends, it only happens on accident. I am just that disorganised. <i>Anyhow</i>, my miraculous timing aside, this was <b>basically the best thing</b> and I am utterly soft for this book. Yessss the romance was a bit fast but like I shall fling all negativity into the sea and just dissolve myself into this book where people can just meet the perfect friend, the perfect girl, and fall so wholly for them that they just click into place. It made my antisocial heart happy. Aw.<br /><br /><b>This book, at its core, is actually about friendship.</b> ngl I am softly crying my love for Kate and Violet and the ruin of Mark and Ryan. But the romance was the beginning, the heart was the friendships. When they break, when they grow, when you meet someone and fall-into-friendship-love with them. When you realise your childhood friend and you don't fit together anymore. When you fall in love with your best friend who doesn't love you back. It's an exploration on so many types of friendship and the aches and love that comes with it and THIS is important. THIS. Ok. <b>Friendship is usually an integral part of being a teen and I think this book so well captures the heartache it can bring -- and also the unimanigable support it is to have someone at your side who <i>knows you</i>. </b><br /><br />[pauses to feel passionately about this]<br /><br /><b>It is also, super queer.</b> Am happy 🤗Mark and Kate both narrate. They're both queer and they do not fall in love -- they just somehow click into a friendship that can carry them through. I loved Kat so hard, with her anxiety and inability to face things. Every time she ran away, I just wanted to run with her. And Mark, with his wholly and consuming love for his closeted-gay best friend who...never loved him back. (Ok but Ryan was a dick, we can admit this a bit. Scared, so I feel for him, but also...ya, a dick.) I loved how the book was honestly about <b>becoming</b>. We're not quite sure what yet? But you can change and become something without knowing where you're going the whole time.<br /><br />UGH emotions. I had many reading this. I 100% recommend it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9279432473870504691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1599291963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599291963" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1599291963?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christine by: </span>
      Larry great review 5
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599291963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6167830645051668423">I would like to thank Net Galley, St. Martin’s Press, and the authors for an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an unbiased review.<br/><br/>Why didn’t they have books like this when I needed them decades ago? You Know Me Well is a YA novel exploring the angst of young LGBT love. Back in the day there was nothing, I repeat nothing, nada, zilch out there for us who were realizing we were different and not understanding why we were “not normal.” Thanks to the changing times, there is now plenty of l</span>
  <span id="freeText6167830645051668423" style="display:none">I would like to thank Net Galley, St. Martin’s Press, and the authors for an advanced copy of this book in exchange for an unbiased review.<br /><br />Why didn’t they have books like this when I needed them decades ago? You Know Me Well is a YA novel exploring the angst of young LGBT love. Back in the day there was nothing, I repeat nothing, nada, zilch out there for us who were realizing we were different and not understanding why we were “not normal.” Thanks to the changing times, there is now plenty of literature available to help young LGBT people come to terms with their sexuality and understand that yes, they ARE normal. Granted, a minority, but normal indeed.<br /><br />You Know Me Well is told from two POVs, those of Mark and Kate. Mark is a junior in high school and a star baseball player. He and his BFF Ryan, a poet and high school classmate, are dating, sort of, but they do not talk about it, not even to each other. Kate has had her eyes on Violet, cousin to her best friend Lehna, for a few years. Kate thinks she is in love with Violet though she really doesn’t know her. One of my early criticisms of the story was that Kate and Violet seemingly fall in love within two seconds of getting together without the reader knowing what this is based on. No foreplay whatsoever! As I read on, however, it dawned on me that their story is not about what drew them together, but about their <i>reactions</i> to their feelings and to the prospect of a long lasting relationship. I thought this was really well done. My only other quibble with the Kate-Violet arc is that these 18 year olds seemed terribly insightful for their age and level of experience.<br /><br />Mark and Ryan’s story has at its center the issue of the lines between platonic and romantic love. There are some very touching scenes in this arc. In my opinion, Mark’s resolution of this situation is way too fast to be believable, but I went with it and loved how it all played out.<br /><br />A lot of themes are touched upon in this novel. The misgivings of coming out are briefly addressed; more detail here would have been nice. Trying to determine the difference between what one is expected to do and how a person really feels about that direction is dealt with in regards to Kate’s higher education and potential art career. A really well done part of both the Kate-Violet arc and the Mark-Ryan arc revolves around being one’s own enemy when fearfulness is allowed to prohibit taking “that next step” in opening one’s self up to new opportunities and challenges. Perhaps the theme I loved best is that of the true gift of a strong platonic relationship where each person will do whatever he or she can to further the best interests of the other. <br /><br />Despite a few flaws, I found this to be a very poignant and satisfying read. I recommend it to all readers of YA and actually also to non YA fans like myself who are looking for a little break from their favorite genre. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6167830645051668423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1459837618" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459837618" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1459837618?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459837618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1800731929852047116">I'm starting to think that David Levithan is my spirit animal. With every one of his books, he just <i>gets</i> me, you know?<br/><br/>Despite the fact that they sit next to each other in their high school calculus class, Mark and Katie have barely spoken to each other. So their official "meet cute" encounter is unlike any you've heard ofKate is hiding in a gay bar at the start of San Francisco's Pride Festival, running away before she gets the chance to meet the girl she's been dreaming about for months, when </span>
  <span id="freeText1800731929852047116" style="display:none">I'm starting to think that David Levithan is my spirit animal. With every one of his books, he just <i>gets</i> me, you know?<br /><br />Despite the fact that they sit next to each other in their high school calculus class, Mark and Katie have barely spoken to each other. So their official "meet cute" encounter is unlike any you've heard ofKate is hiding in a gay bar at the start of San Francisco's Pride Festival, running away before she gets the chance to meet the girl she's been dreaming about for months, when she sees Mark dancing on the bar. In his underwear.<br /><br />Mark, too, is having his share of issues, despite winning the underwear contest. He's only at the bar because his closeted, more-than-best-friend Ryan, wanted to take a risk and go to the Pride Festival this year, and Mark would do anything to be with Ryan. Even if Mark has never told Ryan how he really feels about him. And when Ryan meets another guy, Mark is unsure of what to do, and where he fits in.<br /><br />That night is the catalyst for an intense friendship between Mark and Kate, two people who had always known of, but never truly knew, the other. Mark must confront his feelings for Ryan and make a decision about whether to let his friend follow his own path, regardless of where that leaves him, or fight for what he wants more than anything. And Kate, who is a year older, must confront her own friendships, her fears, her feelings of inadequacy, and her inability to let herself go—even if she would go toward what she has always wanted.<br /><br />Can a person you've never really known get to know you so well in just a short period of time? What does embracing that relationship to its fullest mean for those with whom you have intense, lengthy history? Told in alternating chapters between Kate and Mark's perspectives, <b>
  <i>You Know Me Well</i>
</b> is a book about knowing when to listen to your heart and when to trust your head, knowing whom you can count on and when, and the possibilities of, well, becoming who you truly are.<br /><br />I absolutely loved this book. Obviously I can identify with Mark's character more than Kate's (in more ways than I'd care to divulge), but I found his struggles, his emotions, even his wrong moves more appealing. At first, Kate's inability to tell people how she felt and what she was thinking, which led to chaos with nearly everyone in her life, was a bit frustrating, until she explains why.<br /><br />I have been a fan of Levithan's for years now, and truly devour each of his books (those he writes himself and those he writes with others) in one or two sittings. Nina LaCour's style meshes so well with David's; although I'd assume David wrote Mark's chapters and Nina wrote Kate's, I don't know that to be true, and either way it just worked beautifully. This is a book that made me smile, made me cry (of course), made me grateful for those in my life, and made me a little bitter (I'll admit) that my high school experience couldn't have been this way, but then again, those scars made me the person I am now.<br /><br />NetGalley and St. Martin's Press provided me an advance copy of the book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making this available! <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1800731929852047116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1639173092" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1639173092" />
    <a title="emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10820397-emily"><img alt="emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528807954p2/10820397.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1639173092?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emily" href="/user/show/10820397-emily">emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1639173092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15559490670181690414">I don't really know how to rate this because right now it's 2:30AM and I'm feeling a lot of things, so I'm just going to keep it at 4 stars for now. <br/><br/> *EDIT* it's the next morning, at some point in the night when I was mostly asleep I switched to 5 stars, now I'm going back to 4 be officially saying 4.3..I think. A little more than 4 but not 5. Maybe 4.5? I hate star ratings. Anyway...<br/><br/>I don't think I can write a completely sufficient review of this book at this time, due to things I can't really </span>
  <span id="freeText15559490670181690414" style="display:none">I don't really know how to rate this because right now it's 2:30AM and I'm feeling a lot of things, so I'm just going to keep it at 4 stars for now. <br /><br /> *EDIT* it's the next morning, at some point in the night when I was mostly asleep I switched to 5 stars, now I'm going back to 4 be officially saying 4.3..I think. A little more than 4 but not 5. Maybe 4.5? I hate star ratings. Anyway...<br /><br />I don't think I can write a completely sufficient review of this book at this time, due to things I can't really talk about or express, but I'll try. <br /><br /><i> You Know Me Well </i> was a really refreshing gay YA book. Mark and Kate came out long before this book started, and are totally secure and comfortable in their sexualities. This is not something that I, personally, have come across in the LGBT+ YA that I've read. When it comes to gay teens, their stories have always been coming out stories, about how hard that is and what being in the closet has done to them and their process of telling people or just hiding the gay away. Those can be important stories, but it's not all their stories can be. <i> You Know Me Well </i> provides this wonderful take on gay teens where they have, you know, normal teenage problems because they are <i>normal teenagers</i>. They have fights with friends, doubts about college and their futures, problems with their romantic interests (who just happen to be of the same gender). I just think the fact that this story exists, showing how there is an After once you come out and it can be good no matter what may have happened during the process of, is amazing and wonderful. <br /><br />I think everything I mentioned in the previous paragraph heightens my opinion of this book. If this was about all straight kids, I don't know if I would have liked it as much. The relationship between Mark and Kate was really nice, and I could really, really see myself in Kate a lot of the time (especially in terms of how she reacted to certain situations and the way her thoughts spiraled downward a lot). <i> But </i> some of this book was a little unrealistic. I think it's perfectly believable that Mark and Kate could become friends so quickly, but some of the things they did together and experience in one night and they way that certain events come from that night is pretty unrealistic. The thing is, I don't know if that bothers me or not. I don't know if every single contemporary YA has to be 100% believable and practical all of the time. I think the events that occur in this story just add to this magical feeling I had while reading it, and I think that that's okay. But, again, if it were about straight kids I think it would bother me. There was also a bit of instalove which I'm usually not a fan of, but I'm cool with this brand of gay instalove. <br /><br />There's something just kind of really special and glowing about this book to me, I think that might be something really personal and that everyone might not feel, but <i> You Know Me Well </i> is still definitely a very refreshing and positive take on the gay teen experience that I feel is lacking in the YA world. Also, David Levithan and Nina LaCour are just as fabulous and wonderful as usual. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15559490670181690414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1661301020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1661301020" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10697179-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580549097p2/10697179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1661301020?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/10697179-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=owned">owned</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1661301020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14778594465943609124">I just want to thank St. Martin's Press for sending me a finished copy of this book to read and review! I absolutely LOVED this book so I am SO happy to have a copy I can display!<br/>It also gave me an excuse to pick this up right away when I might not have for a while.<br/><br/>It is not every day that a contemporary YA gets put into my favourites shelf. It is actually my least read genre and now all I can wonder is why? Why don't I read more YA contemporary? Why don't I read more LGBTQ+ fiction? Why have I </span>
  <span id="freeText14778594465943609124" style="display:none">I just want to thank St. Martin's Press for sending me a finished copy of this book to read and review! I absolutely LOVED this book so I am SO happy to have a copy I can display!<br />It also gave me an excuse to pick this up right away when I might not have for a while.<br /><br />It is not every day that a contemporary YA gets put into my favourites shelf. It is actually my least read genre and now all I can wonder is why? Why don't I read more YA contemporary? Why don't I read more LGBTQ+ fiction? Why have I yet to read more David Levithan before now since I loved Every Day so much? And lastly, why have I not picked up anything by Nina Lacour? I don't know the answer to any of these questions, but I am going to be remedying this very quickly!<br /><br />This book follows Mark and Kate and the way their life changes during Pride Week. They meet one night and find they both have things in common and they help each other deal with the things they need to deal with.<br />I thought this book was going to be a love story/romance story. It started out to be that way. But this is not a love story. This is about coming to terms with the person you are, with the things you cannot change, with the feelings you have, or don't have, and it's about learning to be the person that you are. This is also not a story about being gay. It's not a story about coming out, or accepting your sexuality, or being uncomfortable in your skin. This is just a story about 2 LGBTQ+ characters who are dealing with the real world. And it's amazing. The messages in this story were amazing. I have never related to a book so much in my life. Both Kate and Mark are dealing with things that I am dealing with in my life right now and it was like I was getting a speech from my friend helping me through things. <br /><br />I just loved this story. The characters were so well written. The writing was so poetic. I just loved this and I can't wait to come back to this story one day in the future because my heart is full of happiness (and a little bit of sadness at one thing but I'll move on). <br /><br />Just a little end note: I read this book 3 days ago and I have finished 2 novels since then and I am still thinking about this book because I loved it so much. I absolutely recommend reading this as soon as possible. ESPECIALLY since it's pride month and a perfect time and excuse to get to this sooner rather than later.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14778594465943609124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2425819193" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425819193" />
    <a title="Acqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47160872-acqua"><img alt="Acqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548417878p2/47160872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425819193?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Acqua" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Acqua" href="/user/show/47160872-acqua">Acqua</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=db">db</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=love-polygons">love-polygons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=yff">yff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=qf">qf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=q">q</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=qm">qm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425819193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4691335121893067420"><b>There's nothing like happy queer books during Pride month.</b> Especially when said books are set during Pride month themselves.<br/><br/>I loved how queer this was. Every single character but the parents is queer, and there's almost no homophobia. This isn't to say that there's no conflict - I love low-conflict queer romances too, but this isn't exactly one of them - it's just that <b>the conflict is never driven by homophobia</b>.<br/>⇝ <b>Kate</b> has always idealized her best friend's cousin, Violet, but is afraid to get to</span>
  <span id="freeText4691335121893067420" style="display:none"><b>There's nothing like happy queer books during Pride month.</b> Especially when said books are set during Pride month themselves.<br /><br />I loved how queer this was. Every single character but the parents is queer, and there's almost no homophobia. This isn't to say that there's no conflict - I love low-conflict queer romances too, but this isn't exactly one of them - it's just that <b>the conflict is never driven by homophobia</b>.<br />⇝ <b>Kate</b> has always idealized her best friend's cousin, Violet, but is afraid to get to know her. She also tends to "run away" when she's nervous, and she's trying to overcome this.<br />⇝ <b>Mark</b> has been in love with his best friend for years. This book avoids the tired "gay boy is in love with his straight friend" trope; Mark's best friend is a gay boy who just happens to not like him back romantically.<br /><br /><b><i>You Know Me Well</i> is a story about queer romance as much as it is one about friendship and solidarity between queer people</b>. It's the story of how Kate and Violet finally met, but it's also the story of Kate and Mark's friendship, of how it's normal to outgrow your friends and crushes, and it's also about overcoming your fears.<br /><br />The main criticism I've seen is that this book is unrealistic, for two reasons. One of them seems to be that <b>some people think this is too happy, and I don't agree</b> (...why do people love queer tragedy so much. why.) I'm fine with all the supposedly unrealistic happy coincidences if you're writing about Pride month. Also, real life is unpredictable too, so why not?<br />The other reason is that the friendships and romances develop too quickly. This is true, because <i>You Know Me Well</i> is a very short book, but <b>sometimes it's refreshing to read about relationships not cleanly progressing with established story beats</b>. In a way, it feels more real, because it doesn't feel like it's following a scheme (...I often feel this way about romance plotlines). Also, relationships <i>can</i> develop quickly!<br /><br />One thing I didn't fully believe in were the friendships that already existed at the beginning of the book. I felt like I was dropped in the middle of a story - <b>I see the friendship falling apart, but I never saw them when they weren't</b>, so I didn't feel as strongly about them as I wanted to.<br /><br />I also didn't always love the writing. The scenes that were about parades and Pride were beautiful, and I understood the characters, but <b>Kate's and Mark's PoV were very similar, which was confusing</b>. I also wish that more identities apart from gay and lesbian had been represented - yes, the cast was mostly queer, but almost everyone was allocis and gay/lesbian.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4691335121893067420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29599654-kate-girlreading?shelf=lgbtqia-rep">lgbtqia-rep</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2106339673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9052293391600498427">This was such a fantastic read and utterly adorable! <br/>I think what I loved most was the fact that we were almost dropped into the middle of a story already in the process of unfolding. The majority of the characters, having already come out, were happy and secure in their sexualities and relationships were already established, all of which were different but with an equally honest, real feel to them. I loved that although this had a focus around romance, as a reader we got to watch a strong frien</span>
  <span id="freeText9052293391600498427" style="display:none">This was such a fantastic read and utterly adorable! <br />I think what I loved most was the fact that we were almost dropped into the middle of a story already in the process of unfolding. The majority of the characters, having already come out, were happy and secure in their sexualities and relationships were already established, all of which were different but with an equally honest, real feel to them. I loved that although this had a focus around romance, as a reader we got to watch a strong friendship grow as well, which I've not come across a lot in YA. The pride elements were so much fun to read, I especially loved the description of the parades and San Fransisco. I loved that both Kate and Mark were going through different things but were exactly what each other needed to help them get through. They had their separate lives and drama going on but they where always there for each other quietly yet unwaveringly.<br />I also thoroughly enjoyed the writing style. It was incredibly comfortable to read and flowed between the different perspectives brilliantly. I found myself happily flying through it! <br />With friendships, romance, big life decision and a diverse cast of characters, including multiple f/f and m/m romances, gay and lesbian pov's and a genderqueer minor character, this was a refreshing and lovely read.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2906460107" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9990184656564823479"><i> “you’re becoming. you’re in the process of becoming. you just don’t know what yet.” </i><br/><br/>sad to say that i really expected more from this, considering i love both authors, but that left me all the more disappointed in the end. i never really connected to a single character in this book, never felt compelled to read more about them or find out, you know, <i>anything</i>. the only thing that kept me reading was the length, since this is a quite short book. and that is where it went wrong first and foremost. </span>
  <span id="freeText9990184656564823479" style="display:none"><i> “you’re becoming. you’re in the process of becoming. you just don’t know what yet.” </i><br /><br />sad to say that i really expected more from this, considering i love both authors, but that left me all the more disappointed in the end. i never really connected to a single character in this book, never felt compelled to read more about them or find out, you know, <i>anything</i>. the only thing that kept me reading was the length, since this is a quite short book. and that is where it went wrong first and foremost. character and plot development alike could have benefited SO! MUCH! if this book was maybe 50 pages longer. this way, it all felt too crammed.<br /><br />i loved every single aspect about pride and how it played such an essential role in the book, though. also, a large portion of the characters were queer which is just mwah, chef’s kiss. the depiction of queer culture was amazing, but those points were sadly the only things i actually enjoyed. it felt too unrealistic, too unauthentic at times as if it was trying too hard to be something it just wasn’t.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>→ 2.5 stars</b>

<div id="review_1674618602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1674618602" />
    <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay"><img alt="Nicay (dearnicay)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602162853p2/36178759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1674618602?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicay (dearnicay)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicay (dearnicay)" href="/user/show/36178759-nicay-dearnicay">Nicay (dearnicay)</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28261643-you-know-me-well">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674618602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736060402518101650"><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465705811i/19390951.png' width='350' height='100' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>
  <b>DNF at 68%</b>
</i><br/><br/>You know me well is the title of the book and…<br/><br/><i>
  <b>It didn’t end well for me.</b>
</i><br/><br/>I am really sorry. I really tried to finish and liked this one, but I must end this because I know I will be disappointed. It’s the reason of <i>it’s not you, it’s me.</i><br/><br/>The story was focused on the LGBT concept and I am a supporter of this cause, but the story was really tedious. I can’t connect to the characters, which I murmur to myself, <i>was it my fault?</i><br/><br/>It’s only based on my opinion; if you want this one, </span>
  <span id="freeText1736060402518101650" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465705811i/19390951.png" width="350" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br><i>
  <b>DNF at 68%</b>
</i><br><br>You know me well is the title of the book and…<br><br><i>
  <b>It didn’t end well for me.</b>
</i><br><br>I am really sorry. I really tried to finish and liked this one, but I must end this because I know I will be disappointed. It’s the reason of <i>it’s not you, it’s me.</i><br><br>The story was focused on the LGBT concept and I am a supporter of this cause, but the story was really tedious. I can’t connect to the characters, which I murmur to myself, <i>was it my fault?</i><br><br>It’s only based on my opinion; if you want this one, just give it a try. This review was not a hindrance to avoid reading the book. If it didn’t end well for me, maybe you will like it. <br><br><blockquote>
<a href="http://queennicaybooks.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Wordpress</a>┃<a href="http://instagram.com/thenerdysideofaqueen" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ┃ <a href="http://twitter.com/queennicay" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ┃ <a href="http://queennicay.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1455767466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455767466" />
    <a title="Cassandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22224742-cassandra"><img alt="Cassandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476890938p2/22224742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455767466?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassandra" href="/user/show/22224742-cassandra">Cassandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22224742-cassandra?shelf=reads-of-2016">reads-of-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455767466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10081912127952750424"><i>
  <b>"And we step off the curb, all of us together, as if to say, Here we come- through hard days and good ones, through despair and through exhilaration, in love and out of love, for just now or for forever. Here we come. It's out parade."</b>
</i><br/><br/>As made clear by the four star rating, I love this. It's exactly what I expected, maybe even better. Usually Levithan novels deal with deep and even dark topics without lowering the general mood of the novel. this one did that very well. I'm definitely going to</span>
  <span id="freeText10081912127952750424" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"And we step off the curb, all of us together, as if to say, Here we come- through hard days and good ones, through despair and through exhilaration, in love and out of love, for just now or for forever. Here we come. It's out parade."</b>
</i><br /><br />As made clear by the four star rating, I love this. It's exactly what I expected, maybe even better. Usually Levithan novels deal with deep and even dark topics without lowering the general mood of the novel. this one did that very well. I'm definitely going to look into Nina LaCour's books as well, because while her style and his weaved together seamlessly, plot-wise you could see both of their influences. <br /><br />A lot of people were put off by the "insta-friends" situation. In the beginning, I as on board with the critics. Finding someone you know at Pride and then becoming instant besties sounds a bit unrealistic. But thinking through the ways I've met some of my closest friends, I realize that is how some of us form bonds. Especially in a situation like Pride week. Finding someone you can confide in, party with at night, has no chance of ruining the friendship by falling in love with you, and lives close by? I would latch on too. But I do see how some people were bothered by it. I just personally found it a believable miracle.<br /><br />Even though this novel had a bunch of romances, they shared the same amount of spotlight time as the friendships, which I thought was huge. I loved the way Lehna and Kate's friendship was portrayed; because people grow apart, and while they can grow back together, sometimes they don't. Ryan and Mark's issues were so realistic it hurt. I've watched so many people fall in love with a best friend who will never feel the same way, and while yes, we've seen it a million times, I liked how it wasn't the typical "straight friend will never be gay for me problem."<br /><br />I loved Kate and Violet as a couple. It was both hilarious, and just adorable to watch these two try to transition from pen pals to girlfriends. But I will not deny it, Mark and Kate's friendship was a really big part of this book, and so due to that, I loved it with just as much, if not maybe a bit more, than the romances. As was said in this book, but I can't find the exact quote so bare with me, friendship is harder than romance. There's no sex or kissing, just two people who love each other in a way not fueled by hormones.<br /><br />Usually poetry in novels annoys me. Half of the time it's just poorly written since the author themselves isn't a poet, and the other half of the time it just doesn't impress me. This book gained a star from it's poetry slam. The depth it provided to Ryan's character was surreal, because until then, he had really just been "that guy Mark is in love with." The poetry reading provided him with characterization that wasn't manipulated through someone else's memory. <br /><br />The other aspect of the poetry reading that jolted me was Quinn's poem and the characterization it provided an otherwise cliche, and stereotypical side character. I actually struggled to not cry during that scene, because like the characters, I had jumped to conclusions and judged without knowing anything about him. I really hope that like with Tiny Cooper from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a>, he gets a solo novel. I don't know; I just really hope I get to learn more about his character.<br /><br />If you love feel good novels with depth, and lots of adorable characters, this is absolutely for you. Especially if you've read and enjoyed something by the authors before. This book was just good. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10081912127952750424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Justine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7617291-justine"><img alt="Justine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557685507p2/7617291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640596367?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justine" href="/user/show/7617291-justine">Justine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781509823932" href="/book/show/29848950-you-know-me-well">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7617291-justine?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>
