        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640596367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12484810744242513134">I may be biased because... well, David Levithan. But it was such a heartwarming read. I identified with Marc on such a weird level. I'm not a guy and I'm not gay, but love and friendship doesn't know no boundary. And as always, David Levithan knows what to say to make you feel better about a heartbreak. And as always, David Levithan knows how to make you feel better about yourself. And Nina Lacour was a good surprise as well, though I had a few problems with Katie. But towards the end, I really </span>
  <span id="freeText12484810744242513134" style="display:none">I may be biased because... well, David Levithan. But it was such a heartwarming read. I identified with Marc on such a weird level. I'm not a guy and I'm not gay, but love and friendship doesn't know no boundary. And as always, David Levithan knows what to say to make you feel better about a heartbreak. And as always, David Levithan knows how to make you feel better about yourself. And Nina Lacour was a good surprise as well, though I had a few problems with Katie. But towards the end, I really connected with her and loved her for making the right decisions for herself. And I like that Nina Lacour dealt with issues such as not knowing what to do right after high school and how long friendships can come to an end. <br /><br />This book has powerful messages about teen love, about friendship, about life that goes on and life that has to be figured out. </span>

  <span id="freeText15138477097133059659" style="display:none">I love Nina's words and will greedily look for all of her books. I requested this book on her name alone, I didn't even read the synopsis first. <br /><br />I loved Katie and Mark. I loved how they struggled with their similar-but-different situations.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2675644585" />
    <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz"><img alt="Lauren Lanz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586150400p2/82987361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2675644585?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren Lanz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren Lanz" href="/user/show/82987361-lauren-lanz">Lauren Lanz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82987361-lauren-lanz?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2675644585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2592822661476088217">4.5 stars 💘<br/><br/>Opening a book and jumping immediately into a pride parade is exactly as amazing as it sounds 🌈<br/><br/>Kate and Mark have been sitting next to each other in calculus for a year, except they’ve never really noticed it. That is, until Kate spots a familiar face at the local pride parade, which is in fact the boy she’s been sitting next to and knows absolutely nothing about. Mark is falling in love with his best friend Ryan, struggling with the thought that he doesn’t feel the same. Kate is fall</span>
  <span id="freeText2592822661476088217" style="display:none">4.5 stars 💘<br /><br />Opening a book and jumping immediately into a pride parade is exactly as amazing as it sounds 🌈<br /><br />Kate and Mark have been sitting next to each other in calculus for a year, except they’ve never really noticed it. That is, until Kate spots a familiar face at the local pride parade, which is in fact the boy she’s been sitting next to and knows absolutely nothing about. Mark is falling in love with his best friend Ryan, struggling with the thought that he doesn’t feel the same. Kate is falling in love with a girl she’s barely met, hoping to see her again. Mark and Kate have more in common than they could’ve ever have realized, they don’t take very long to become good friends, and this is a story of just that.<br /><br />There’s a certain bliss that reading the first chapter of <i>You Know Me Well</i> gave off, and that happy feeling lingered in the background the entire time. -Except for the fact that I spent a good portion of the book teary eyed. <br /><br />There are certain scenes that had the perfect amount of heart, meaning my poor little emotions were done for. This is a book I can see queer youth living for, especially since it deals largely with both the beautiful and hard things.<br /><br />Our two main perspectives, Mark and Kate, are characters I can see so many teens relating to. You Know Me Well was a lovely story of friendship and romance, everything in between. It’s not too long and definitely worth your time &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="2592822661476088217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1455267567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455267567" />
    <a title="Jess " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27226276-jess"><img alt="Jess " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464321387p2/27226276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455267567?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess " href="/user/show/27226276-jess">Jess </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27226276-jess?shelf=coming-out-2016">coming-out-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27226276-jess?shelf=wish-upon-a-star">wish-upon-a-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455267567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16198205784158841506">Absolutely in love with this book. Majority, if not all, characters are queer. What a perfect book for Pride Month and for me right now. Sometimes books don't need happy endings. Realistic fiction--of beginnings and endings and everything in between. A plathora of emotions. RISK. Characters are flawed and imperfect and that is what makes them perfect and relatable. This is such a word vomit because it's 12:23am but I promise, this is a book to look out for. I suggest everyone, especially the eme</span>
  <span id="freeText16198205784158841506" style="display:none">Absolutely in love with this book. Majority, if not all, characters are queer. What a perfect book for Pride Month and for me right now. Sometimes books don't need happy endings. Realistic fiction--of beginnings and endings and everything in between. A plathora of emotions. RISK. Characters are flawed and imperfect and that is what makes them perfect and relatable. This is such a word vomit because it's 12:23am but I promise, this is a book to look out for. I suggest everyone, especially the emerging young adults (not just emerging as queer, but emerging into the adult life) reads this. Bravo, LaCour and Levithan. Thank you. Genuinely. <br /><br />Edit: This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://princessicaofbooks.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Princessica of Books</a>.<br /><br />*Thank you so much to St. Martin’s Griffin for the complimentary review copy! This in no way affects my review; all opinions are my own.*<br /><br />I am absolutely in love with You Know Me Well by Nina LaCour and David Levithan. It’s not a “AHH, EVERYONE MUST READ” book, but it’s definitely a subtle and appreciative 5-star. The story of friendship at first sight is beautifully told by two LGBTQ advocates, supported with the theme of risk. This is not a cliche, and this is absolutely beautiful.<br /><br />More often than not, the first male and or female the other encounters is the love interest of the story. However, that is not the case in You Know Me Well. It’s completely platonic and also completely refreshing. The dual POVs only heighten the distinct characters of Mark and Kate.<br /><br />They don’t fall in love romantically because both Mark and Kate are gay. In fact, the majority of the characters are queer and I really appreciate that. Both LaCour and Levithan covered the topic wonderfully and also kind of hilariously. None of the characters are your stereotypical gay. In You Know Me Well, gay is the new straight. Even more, I relate to both the characters in some way: Kate’s tendency to run away from things and Mark’s pain. Mark and Kate are distinct characters in relation to each other, but they are also relatable.<br /><br />What I appreciate even more is that we go through all the stages: coming out, accepting oneself, unrequited love, and tragic love. All these events create a plethora of emotions. It’s sad, I’m not going to lie. But, it’s also very beautiful and demonstrates how not all books have happy endings but it’s okay.<br /><br />Finally, the writing style is absolutely beautiful. LaCour’s and Levithan’s writing styles are similar to each other and it’s apparent how much they worked together on this. I’ve always admired LaCour’s writing style and my love for it has only heightened. There is also a scene where there is a poetry slam and it really speaks to my word-loving heart. They are real and raw. And I admire them so much.<br /><br />In other words,<br /><br />You Know Me Well impresses me and it’s the perfect book for Pride Month. The characters are flawed and imperfect but that is what makes them relatable. Maybe it’s the setting of my home town of San Francisco, maybe because You Know Me Well is just plain awesome, maybe because LaCour’s and Levithan’s writing shakes me, and more than likely for all three reasons, I am giving this a wonderful and well-deserved 5-stars.<br /><br />Final rating: ✮✮✮✮✮ (5 stars)<br />How much do I recommend it? I highly recommend it, perfect book for Pride Month, and just perfect book to read of you want to learn more about GLBTQ.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16198205784158841506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VVDZorBIscwacoX6rLMZiRhdbqqSLTLOjnSzSC/AafVstWP1oCfpN92JAhFv9PiEs8FGmRRGu0hDrv64fcjdng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4tvnWwCNuJTfN9tKcDBR67UxOMUcX8Zxbs1ZQ1cwwnzbPl0MEOLgbxjMXKGzd7DmHq0Q9po0T/ejFxSzBTh2Fw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour">About Nina LaCour</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2889003.Nina_LaCour"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1282077633p3/2889003.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10934919268595222400">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br/><br/>Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br/><br/>“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a clas</span>
  <span id="freeText10934919268595222400" style="display:none">Nina LaCour grew up in the San Francisco Bay Area. Her first job was at fourteen in an independent bookstore, and she has since worked in two others. She has tutored and taught in various places, from a juvenile hall to a private college. She now teaches English at an independent high school.<br /><br />Of Hold Still, Nina says:<br /><br />“This book is about loss, and it’s also about art. The loss part comes from a classmate’s suicide. I didn’t know him well, but learning of his death remains one of the most profoundly sad and confusing events of my teenage years. The art part comes from my mother, a high school photography teacher. A girl in one of her student’s photographs inspired the character of Ingrid. While I was writing, I learned how to develop and print black-and-white photographs in a darkroom.”<br /><br />Nina lives in Oakland, California with her wife and their two cute cats. Visit her online at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.ninalacour.com">www.ninalacour.com</a>.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10934919268595222400" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
